📖 개념 학습 (5문항)
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_01concrete
What Is a Two-Step Problem?
A two-step problem requires two operations to solve. You must complete Step 1 first, then use that result for Step 2. The operations can be: +, −, ×, or ÷ in any combination. Example: 'Jake has 5 bags of 6 apples. He eats 3. How many left?' Step 1: 5 × 6 = 30 (find total) Step 2: 30 − 3 = 27 (subtract eaten)
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_02concrete
Bar Model for Two Steps
Draw a bar model to organize a two-step problem. Example: 'Amy has 24 beads. She buys 12 more, then shares them equally among 6 friends.' Bar 1: 24 + 12 = 36 (total beads) Bar 2: 36 ÷ 6 = 6 (each friend gets) The bar model shows what you know and what you need to find.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_03pictorial
Write One Equation for Two Steps
You can write both steps as one equation using parentheses: '(5 × 6) − 3 = n' Solve inside parentheses first: 5 × 6 = 30 Then: 30 − 3 = 27, so n = 27. Parentheses tell you which operation to do FIRST.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_04pictorial
Identify the Operations
To solve any two-step problem, ask: 1. What do I need to find? 2. What information do I have? 3. What happens FIRST? (Step 1 operation) 4. What happens SECOND? (Step 2 operation) Common patterns: × then − (find total, then remove) ÷ then + (split into groups, then add) + then ÷ (combine, then share) × then + (multiply, then add extra)
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_05abstract
Check Your Answer
After solving a two-step problem, always check: 1. Did I complete BOTH steps? 2. Does my answer make sense with the story? 3. Did I use the right operations? Example check: 'Kim gets 6 stickers each. Does 6 make sense if she started with 24 and gave 6 away?' → 24−6=18, 18÷3=6 ✓

TRYTRY_013.OA.D.8난이도 2
A class has 28 pencils. The teacher buys 12 more, then divides them equally among 8 students. How many pencils does each student get?
  • A) 4
  • B) 5 ✓
  • C) 6
  • D) 7
예상 함정
A: partial_answerStopping at intermediate result 3.OA.D.8.M01
C: irrelevant_info_usedUsing all numbers including irrelevant ones 3.OA.D.8.M02
D: operation_keyword_misreadMisinterpreting relational language (more/fewer/less) 3.OA.D.8.M03
💡 Step 1: add the pencils together first. Step 2: divide the total by 8 students. / What happens first? Adding! Then dividing.
풀이
  1. 28 + 12 = 40
  2. 40 ÷ 8 = 5

📖 개념 학습 (5문항)
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_01concrete
What Is the Order of Operations?
When an expression has more than one operation, you need rules to know which to do first. Without rules, different people get different answers! The order of operations gives everyone the same result.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_02concrete
Multiply Before You Add
Look at 3 + 4 × 2. If you add first: 3 + 4 = 7, then 7 × 2 = 14 (wrong!). If you multiply first: 4 × 2 = 8, then 3 + 8 = 11 (correct!). Always multiply or divide before you add or subtract.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_03pictorial
Parentheses Change the Answer
Adding parentheses can change the result completely. Compare: 2 + 3 × 4 = 2 + 12 = 14 (no parentheses — multiply first). But (2 + 3) × 4 = 5 × 4 = 20 (parentheses first — different answer!).
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_04pictorial
Division Before Subtraction
Division also comes before addition and subtraction. In 20 − 15 ÷ 3: divide first → 15 ÷ 3 = 5. Then subtract → 20 − 5 = 15. If you subtract first you get the wrong answer.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_05abstract
Label Each Step
When an expression is complex, label every step: Step 1 — Parentheses, Step 2 — × or ÷, Step 3 — + or −. Example: 2 + 3 × (8 − 2). Step 1: 8 − 2 = 6. Step 2: 3 × 6 = 18. Step 3: 2 + 18 = 20.

If 2 × 6 = 12, then 12 ÷ 2 = ?

💡 Division splits a total into equal groups. Use the inverse multiplication fact.
candidates: 3.OA.A.3.M01, 3.OA.A.3.M02, 3.OA.A.3.M03, 3.OA.A.3.M04, 3.OA.A.3.M05, 3.OA.A.3.M06, 3.OA.A.3.M07
📖 개념 학습 (5문항)
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_01concrete
Dividing by 2
Dividing by 2 is the same as finding half. 10 ÷ 2 = 5 because half of 10 is 5. You split one group into exactly 2 equal parts.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_02concrete
Use Doubles
If you know 2 × 8 = 16, then 16 ÷ 2 = 8. Doubles facts help you divide by 2 quickly. Think: 2 × ? = 16 → ? = 8.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_03pictorial
Model It with Two Groups
To find 14 ÷ 2: draw 2 circles. Deal 14 counters one by one, alternating circles. Each circle gets 7. So 14 ÷ 2 = 7.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_04pictorial
Halving on a Number Line
On a number line, 12 ÷ 2 = 6 means: start at 12, make jumps of 2 going back. Count: 12→10→8→6→4→2→0 — that's 6 jumps. So 12 ÷ 2 = 6.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_05abstract
The Halving Rule
Dividing by 2 always gives you half the number. Half of 18 = 9, so 18 ÷ 2 = 9. You can also think of it as: 2 × quotient = dividend. This works for ALL even numbers.

📖 개념 학습 (5문항)
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_01concrete
Dividing by 10
When you divide a multiple of 10 by 10, just drop the zero. 70 ÷ 10 = 7. Think: 10 groups of 7 = 70, so 70 ÷ 10 = 7.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_02concrete
Use ×10 Facts
If 10 × 6 = 60, then 60 ÷ 10 = 6. Use your multiplication table of 10 in reverse. Think: 10 × ? = 60 → ? = 6.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_03pictorial
Skip Count Back by 10
Count back by 10s from 50: 50, 40, 30, 20, 10, 0 — 5 jumps. So 50 ÷ 10 = 5. Each jump back represents one group of 10.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_04pictorial
Number Line: Divide by 10
For 40 ÷ 10: start at 40, make jumps of 10 back to 0. Count: 40→30→20→10→0 — that's 4 jumps. So 40 ÷ 10 = 4. Each jump = one group of 10.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_05abstract
The Drop-the-Zero Rule
For any multiple of 10: n×10 ÷ 10 = n. Just remove the trailing zero. 10÷10=1, 20÷10=2, 30÷10=3, ... 90÷10=9, 100÷10=10. This works because 10 groups of n = 10n, so 10n÷10 = n.
🔧 시도 (5문항)
🚩 mark

📖 개념 학습 (5문항)
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_01concrete
Dividing by 5
Count by 5s to find the quotient. For 35 ÷ 5: count 5, 10, 15, 20, 25, 30, 35 — that's 7 counts. So 35 ÷ 5 = 7.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_02concrete
Use ×5 Facts
If 5 × 8 = 40, then 40 ÷ 5 = 8. Use your multiplication table of 5 in reverse. Think: 5 × ? = 40 → ? = 8.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_03pictorial
Think of Nickels
Each nickel is 5¢. 25¢ ÷ 5¢ = 5 nickels. To find how many nickels make 45¢: count by 5s to 45 → 5, 10, 15, 20, 25, 30, 35, 40, 45 → 9 counts. 45 ÷ 5 = 9 nickels.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_04pictorial
Number Line: Divide by 5
For 45 ÷ 5: start at 45, jump back by 5 until you reach 0. Count: 45→40→35→30→25→20→15→10→5→0 — 9 jumps. So 45 ÷ 5 = 9.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_05abstract
The ÷5 Pattern
All ÷5 quotients: 5÷5=1, 10÷5=2, 15÷5=3, 20÷5=4, 25÷5=5, 30÷5=6, 35÷5=7, 40÷5=8, 45÷5=9, 50÷5=10. Notice: each dividend ends in 0 or 5, and each quotient increases by 1.

candidates: 3.OA.C.7.M01, 3.OA.C.7.M02, 3.OA.C.7.M03, 3.OA.C.7.M04, 3.OA.C.7.M05, 3.OA.C.7.M06, 3.OA.C.7.M07
📖 개념 학습 (5문항)
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_01concrete
Sharing Into 3 Equal Groups
When you divide by 3, you share a total equally among 3 groups. Example: 12 counters shared into 3 groups → each group gets 4. So 12 ÷ 3 = 4.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_02concrete
Array: 3 Rows
An array with 3 rows helps you see ÷3. A 3×8 array has 24 tiles. Reading across rows: 24 ÷ 3 = 8. Each row is a group of 8.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_03pictorial
Draw 3 Circles and Distribute
To solve 18 ÷ 3: draw 3 circles (groups). Deal 18 counters one at a time — 1 to circle 1, 1 to circle 2, 1 to circle 3, repeat. Each circle ends up with 6. So 18 ÷ 3 = 6.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_04pictorial
Number Line: Backward Jumps of 3
To find 27 ÷ 3, start at 27 on a number line and hop backward by 3 each time: 27 → 24 → 21 → 18 → 15 → 12 → 9 → 6 → 3 → 0. Count the hops: 9 hops. So 27 ÷ 3 = 9.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_05abstract
The ÷3 Pattern: Reverse the ×3 Fact
Every ×3 fact gives you a ÷3 fact: 3×1=3 → 3÷3=1 3×2=6 → 6÷3=2 3×3=9 → 9÷3=3 3×4=12 → 12÷3=4 3×5=15 → 15÷3=5 3×6=18 → 18÷3=6 3×7=21 → 21÷3=7 3×8=24 → 24÷3=8 3×9=27 → 27÷3=9 3×10=30 → 30÷3=10 Strategy: think '3 × ? = dividend' to find the quotient.

candidates: 3.OA.C.7.M01, 3.OA.C.7.M02, 3.OA.C.7.M03, 3.OA.C.7.M04, 3.OA.C.7.M05, 3.OA.C.7.M06, 3.OA.C.7.M07
📖 개념 학습 (5문항)
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_01concrete
Sharing Into 4 Equal Groups
When you divide by 4, you share a total equally among 4 groups. Example: 24 counters shared into 4 groups → each group gets 6. So 24 ÷ 4 = 6.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_02concrete
Halve Twice Strategy
Dividing by 4 is the same as halving twice. Try with 20: Step 1: 20 ÷ 2 = 10 (first half) Step 2: 10 ÷ 2 = 5 (half again) Result: 20 ÷ 4 = 5. This works because 4 = 2 × 2.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_03pictorial
Relate to ×4 Multiplication
Draw 4 rows of 9 dots — that is a 4×9 array showing 36 total. Reading it as division: 36 dots in 4 rows means 36 ÷ 4 = 9 dots per row. Every ×4 fact gives a ÷4 fact.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_04pictorial
Number Line: Backward Jumps of 4
To find 36 ÷ 4, start at 36 on a number line and hop backward by 4 each time: 36 → 32 → 28 → 24 → 20 → 16 → 12 → 8 → 4 → 0. Count the hops: 9 hops. So 36 ÷ 4 = 9.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_05abstract
The ÷4 Pattern: Reverse the ×4 Fact
Every ×4 fact gives you a ÷4 fact: 4×1=4 → 4÷4=1 4×2=8 → 8÷4=2 4×3=12 → 12÷4=3 4×4=16 → 16÷4=4 4×5=20 → 20÷4=5 4×6=24 → 24÷4=6 4×7=28 → 28÷4=7 4×8=32 → 32÷4=8 4×9=36 → 36÷4=9 4×10=40 → 40÷4=10 Strategy: think '4 × ? = dividend' to find the quotient.

PTPT_053.OA.C.7난이도 1
36 eggs are packed 6 per carton. How many cartons?
  • A) 5
  • B) 6 ✓
  • C) 7
  • D) 8

D: five_pattern_overgeneralizedThinks all ×5 products end in 5 (or 0) but applies wrong digit 3.OA.C.7.M03
💡 Divide the total by the size of each group to find the number of groups.
candidates: 3.OA.C.7.M01, 3.OA.C.7.M02, 3.OA.C.7.M03, 3.OA.C.7.M04, 3.OA.C.7.M05, 3.OA.C.7.M06, 3.OA.C.7.M07
📖 개념 학습 (5문항)
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_01concrete
Sharing Into 6 Equal Groups
When you divide by 6, you share a total equally among 6 groups. Example: 36 counters shared into 6 groups → each group gets 6. So 36 ÷ 6 = 6.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_02concrete
Array: 6 Rows
A 6×8 array has 48 tiles arranged in 6 rows of 8. Reading it as division: 48 tiles in 6 rows means 48 ÷ 6 = 8 tiles per row. The ×6 fact 6×8=48 gives the ÷6 fact 48÷6=8.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_03pictorial
Break ÷6 Into ÷2 Then ÷3
Since 6 = 2 × 3, dividing by 6 is the same as dividing by 2 and then by 3. Example: 24 ÷ 6 Step 1: 24 ÷ 2 = 12 Step 2: 12 ÷ 3 = 4 Result: 24 ÷ 6 = 4. Check: 6 × 4 = 24 ✓
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_04pictorial
Number Line: Backward Jumps of 6
To find 48 ÷ 6, start at 48 on a number line and hop backward by 6 each time: 48 → 42 → 36 → 30 → 24 → 18 → 12 → 6 → 0. Count the hops: 8 hops. So 48 ÷ 6 = 8.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_05abstract
The ÷6 Pattern: Reverse the ×6 Fact
Every ×6 fact gives you a ÷6 fact: 6×1=6 → 6÷6=1 6×2=12 → 12÷6=2 6×3=18 → 18÷6=3 6×4=24 → 24÷6=4 6×5=30 → 30÷6=5 6×6=36 → 36÷6=6 6×7=42 → 42÷6=7 6×8=48 → 48÷6=8 6×9=54 → 54÷6=9 6×10=60 → 60÷6=10 Strategy: think '6 × ? = dividend' to find the quotient.
🔧 시도 (5문항)

candidates: 3.OA.C.7.M01, 3.OA.C.7.M02, 3.OA.C.7.M03, 3.OA.C.7.M04, 3.OA.C.7.M05, 3.OA.C.7.M06, 3.OA.C.7.M07
📖 개념 학습 (5문항)
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_01concrete
Sharing Into 7 Equal Groups
When you divide by 7, you share a total equally among 7 groups. Example: 21 counters shared into 7 groups → each group gets 3. So 21 ÷ 7 = 3.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_02concrete
Array: 7 Rows
A 7×8 array has 56 tiles arranged in 7 rows of 8. Reading it as division: 56 tiles in 7 rows means 56 ÷ 7 = 8 tiles per row. The ×7 fact 7×8=56 gives the ÷7 fact 56÷7=8.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_03pictorial
Days and Weeks
There are 7 days in a week. So dividing a number of days by 7 gives the number of weeks. Examples: 7 days = 7÷7 = 1 week 14 days = 14÷7 = 2 weeks 21 days = 21÷7 = 3 weeks 35 days = 35÷7 = 5 weeks This real-world context helps you remember ÷7 facts.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_04pictorial
Number Line: Backward Jumps of 7
To find 63 ÷ 7, start at 63 on a number line and hop backward by 7 each time: 63 → 56 → 49 → 42 → 35 → 28 → 21 → 14 → 7 → 0. Count the hops: 9 hops. So 63 ÷ 7 = 9.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_05abstract
The ÷7 Pattern: Reverse the ×7 Fact
Every ×7 fact gives you a ÷7 fact: 7×1=7 → 7÷7=1 7×2=14 → 14÷7=2 7×3=21 → 21÷7=3 7×4=28 → 28÷7=4 7×5=35 → 35÷7=5 7×6=42 → 42÷7=6 7×7=49 → 49÷7=7 7×8=56 → 56÷7=8 7×9=63 → 63÷7=9 7×10=70 → 70÷7=10 Strategy: think '7 × ? = dividend' to find the quotient.

📖 개념 학습 (5문항)
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_01concrete
Sharing Into 8 Equal Groups
When you divide by 8, you share a total equally among 8 groups. Example: 48 counters shared into 8 groups → each group gets 6. So 48 ÷ 8 = 6.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_02concrete
Halve Three Times Strategy
Dividing by 8 is the same as halving three times (because 8 = 2×2×2). Example: 24 ÷ 8 Step 1: 24 ÷ 2 = 12 Step 2: 12 ÷ 2 = 6 Step 3: 6 ÷ 2 = 3 Result: 24 ÷ 8 = 3. Check: 8 × 3 = 24 ✓
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_03pictorial
Array: 8 Rows
A 8×9 array has 72 tiles arranged in 8 rows of 9. Reading it as division: 72 tiles in 8 rows means 72 ÷ 8 = 9 tiles per row. The ×8 fact 8×9=72 gives the ÷8 fact 72÷8=9.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_04pictorial
Number Line: Backward Jumps of 8
To find 72 ÷ 8, start at 72 on a number line and hop backward by 8 each time: 72 → 64 → 56 → 48 → 40 → 32 → 24 → 16 → 8 → 0. Count the hops: 9 hops. So 72 ÷ 8 = 9.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_05abstract
The ÷8 Pattern: Reverse the ×8 Fact
Every ×8 fact gives you a ÷8 fact: 8×1=8 → 8÷8=1 8×2=16 → 16÷8=2 8×3=24 → 24÷8=3 8×4=32 → 32÷8=4 8×5=40 → 40÷8=5 8×6=48 → 48÷8=6 8×7=56 → 56÷8=7 8×8=64 → 64÷8=8 8×9=72 → 72÷8=9 8×10=80 → 80÷8=10 Strategy: think '8 × ? = dividend' to find the quotient.

PTPT_053.OA.C.7난이도 1
81 beads are strung into 9 equal necklaces. How many beads each?
  • A) 7
  • B) 8
  • C) 9 ✓
  • D) 10

D: five_pattern_overgeneralizedThinks all ×5 products end in 5 (or 0) but applies wrong digit 3.OA.C.7.M03
💡 Divide the total into equal groups.
candidates: 3.OA.C.7.M01, 3.OA.C.7.M02, 3.OA.C.7.M03, 3.OA.C.7.M04, 3.OA.C.7.M05, 3.OA.C.7.M06, 3.OA.C.7.M07
📖 개념 학습 (5문항)
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_01concrete
Sharing Into 9 Equal Groups
When you divide by 9, you share a total equally among 9 groups. Example: 54 counters shared into 9 groups → each group gets 6. So 54 ÷ 9 = 6.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_02concrete
Array: 9 Rows
A 9×8 array has 72 tiles arranged in 9 rows of 8. Reading it as division: 72 tiles in 9 rows means 72 ÷ 9 = 8 tiles per row. The ×9 fact 9×8=72 gives the ÷9 fact 72÷9=8.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_03pictorial
Digit-Sum Trick for Multiples of 9
Every multiple of 9 has digits that add up to 9. This helps you check ÷9 answers: 9×1=9 → digits: 9 ✓ 9×2=18 → 1+8=9 ✓ 9×3=27 → 2+7=9 ✓ 9×4=36 → 3+6=9 ✓ 9×5=45 → 4+5=9 ✓ 9×6=54 → 5+4=9 ✓ 9×7=63 → 6+3=9 ✓ 9×8=72 → 7+2=9 ✓ 9×9=81 → 8+1=9 ✓
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_04pictorial
Number Line: Backward Jumps of 9
To find 81 ÷ 9, start at 81 on a number line and hop backward by 9 each time: 81 → 72 → 63 → 54 → 45 → 36 → 27 → 18 → 9 → 0. Count the hops: 9 hops. So 81 ÷ 9 = 9.
🚩 mark
LEARNLN_05abstract
The ÷9 Pattern: Reverse the ×9 Fact
Every ×9 fact gives you a ÷9 fact: 9×1=9 → 9÷9=1 9×2=18 → 18÷9=2 9×3=27 → 27÷9=3 9×4=36 → 36÷9=4 9×5=45 → 45÷9=5 9×6=54 → 54÷9=6 9×7=63 → 63÷9=7 9×8=72 → 72÷9=8 9×9=81 → 81÷9=9 9×10=90 → 90÷9=10 Strategy: think '9 × ? = dividend' to find the quotient.
